The output of slicer <b>38</b> may be a relatively high data rate electrical data stream. Components such as a training deframer may receive the output of slicer <b>38</b>. A forward-error correction (FEC) decoder, if FEC is utilized, may receive the output of the training deframer and may decode the electrical data stream for further transmission downstream (e.g., to the one or more switches and routers after deserialization). The training deframer and FEC decoder may be part of modem <b>16</b>, or external to modem <b>16</b> and are not illustrated for purposes of clarity.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0076\" num=\"0075\">As illustrated, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A receives one pair of the I/Q digitized data streams (i.e., I<sub>1 </sub>and Q<sub>1 </sub>data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A and <b>20</b>B), and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B receives another pair of the I/Q data streams (i.e., I<sub>2 </sub>and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>C and <b>20</b>D). CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B implement a complex filter on received digital electrical data streams to compensate for optical distortion that is represented electrically on the digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0077\" num=\"0076\">For example, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B compensate for chromatic dispersion of optical link <b>24</b>. For instance, if photonics module <b>14</b> receives an optical signal in a long haul application (e.g., from a transmitter that is many miles away), the digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may suffer from chromatic dispersion. This chromatic dispersion is an example of optical distortion that is part of the received optical signal, which CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B compensate for.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0078\" num=\"0077\">As one example, the chromatic dispersion may cause inter-symbol-interference (ISI). In this case, because of the ISI, the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may not be identical to the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>digital electrical data streams that are used to generate the transmitted optical signal that photonics module <b>14</b> receives. To compensate for the chromatic dispersion, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B may be finite impulse response (FIR) filters.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0079\" num=\"0078\">The number of taps for the FIR filters of CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B may be proportional to the effective sampling rate of the digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D (e.g., proportional to the number of samples that need to be processed per second). Accordingly, reducing the number of samples that need to be processed per second with digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D allows for a reduction in the number of taps for the FIR filters of CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B, while achieving the same amount of chromatic dispersion compensation. Reducing the number of taps for the FIR filters of CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B reduces the size and the amount of power consumed. For example, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B may potentially be the largest components of modem <b>16</b>, and may also consume the most amount of power. By reducing the number of samples that need to be processed per second rate with digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D, the size of CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B and the amount of power consumed by CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B may be reduced.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0080\" num=\"0079\">In some alternate examples, it may be possible to configure CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B to include the same number of taps for the FIR filters as for instances where the number of samples that need to be processed per second is not reduced. Even in these alternate examples, it may be beneficial to include digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D to reduce the number of samples that need to be processed per second. For instance, in these alternate examples, it may be possible to achieve better chromatic dispersion compensation by reducing the number of samples that need to be processed per second with digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D and compensating for the chromatic dispersion using CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B that include the same number of taps for the FIR filters as examples where the number of samples that need to be processed per second is not reduced.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0081\" num=\"0080\">Timing recovery unit <b>30</b> receives data streams from CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B and performs timing recovery. For example, timing recovery unit <b>30</b> performs symbol timing utilizing interpolation and Timing Error Detector (TED) to achieve symbol timing recovery, although other timing recovery techniques are possible. One example of the timing recovery technique is described in F. M. Gardner, “BPSK/QPSK Timing-Error Detector for Sampled Receivers,” IEEE Transactions on Communications, vol. COM-34, No. 5, May 1986, and is incorporated by reference in its entirety.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0082\" num=\"0081\">The sampling frequency locked clock, generated by timing recovery unit <b>30</b>, may provide the clock signal for components of modem <b>16</b> or for other components on line card <b>12</b>. In some examples, timing recovery unit <b>30</b> may upsample the digital electrical data streams received from CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B so that the number of samples that need to be processed per second of the digital electrical data streams is greater than the effective sampling rate; however, such upsampling is not be required in every example.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0083\" num=\"0082\">Equalizer <b>32</b> receives the data streams from timing recovery unit <b>30</b> and performs any other compensations. For example, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and CD equalizer <b>28</b>B may not be able to compensate for all of the chromatic dispersion, and equalizer <b>32</b> may compensate for any remaining chromatic dispersion. In addition, equalizer <b>32</b> may un-mix the polarization of the received data streams. For example, equalizer <b>32</b> may compensate for any polarization mixing in optical link <b>24</b> (e.g., mixing between the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> and the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0084\" num=\"0083\">Carrier phase estimation unit (CPE) <b>34</b> and carrier frequency estimation unit (CFE) <b>36</b> fix the phase and the frequency offset (between the signal and the local oscillator) of the data stream. For example, photonics module <b>14</b> may include a free-running local oscillator used to recover the optical I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams. Because the local oscillator may be a free-running oscillator, the I<sub>1 </sub>and Q<sub>1 </sub>data streams may be orthogonal to one another, and the I<sub>2 </sub>and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams may be orthogonal to one another; however, the phases of each of these data streams may not be fixed. CPE <b>34</b> and CFE <b>36</b> function in feedback to estimate the relative frequency and phase between the received signal and the local oscillator to track the phase of the data streams. Slicer <b>38</b> receives the data streams from CPE <b>34</b> and digitizes to binary sequences the data streams for further transmission to other components within modem <b>16</b> or other components on line card <b>12</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0085\" num=\"0084\"><figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 3</figref> is a block illustrating another example of downstream hardware units of the modem of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 1</figref> in greater detail. Similar to <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 2</figref>, downstream hardware units <b>22</b>, in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 3</figref>, include CD equalizer <b>28</b>A, CD equalizer <b>28</b>B, timing recover unit <b>30</b>, equalizer <b>32</b>, CPE <b>34</b>, CFE <b>36</b>, and slicer <b>38</b>. These units are substantially similar to the corresponding units illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 2</figref>, and are not discussed further with respect to <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 3</figref>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0086\" num=\"0085\">As illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 3</figref>, downstream hardware units <b>22</b> also includes digital filter <b>40</b>, which is coupled to timing recover unit <b>30</b> and equalizer <b>32</b>. Digital filter <b>40</b> may be similar to digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D. However, digital filter <b>40</b> receives digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate, as reduced by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D, and further reduces the effective sampling rate to a rate that is greater than or equal to the symbol rate. For example, similar to above, assume the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receive is R, and ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the received analog electrical data streams at 2*R. In this example, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may achieve an effective sampling rate 5/4*R for the outputted digital data streams. Digital filter <b>40</b> may further filter the data stream and output a data stream with a further reduced effective sampling rate of R, or a rate greater than R and less than 5/4*R.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0087\" num=\"0086\">In the example illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 3</figref>, it may be possible to further reduce the number of samples that need to be processed per second from the output of timing recover unit <b>30</b>, while leaving sufficient samples to properly recover the magnitude and phase information of the received optical signal to decode the transmitted data. In this manner, the number of samples that need to be processed per second by equalizer <b>32</b>, CPE <b>34</b>, CFE <b>36</b>, and slicer <b>38</b> may be further reduced with digital filter <b>40</b>, which promotes further reduction in the size of equalizer <b>32</b>, CPE <b>34</b>, CFE <b>36</b>, and slicer <b>38</b>, and the amount of power consumed by equalizer <b>32</b>, CPE <b>34</b>, CFE <b>36</b>, and slicer <b>38</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0088\" num=\"0087\"><figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 4</figref> is a block diagram illustrating an example of upstream hardware units of the modem of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 1</figref> in greater detail. As described above, modem <b>16</b> receives downstream data from network <b>26</b> that modem <b>16</b> forwards to routers and switches. In the reverse, modem <b>16</b> receives upstream data from the routers and switches that modem <b>16</b> transmits to network <b>26</b>. <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 4</figref> illustrates examples of upstream hardware units <b>42</b> of modem <b>16</b> that transmit received data to photonics module <b>14</b> for transmission to network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0089\" num=\"0088\">Upstream hardware units <b>42</b> include symbol mapper <b>44</b> and digital to analog converters (DACs) <b>46</b>A-<b>46</b>B. Symbol mapper <b>44</b> may receive a forward-error coded (FEC) encoded data stream that has been framed by a training framer. The training framer may be part of modem <b>16</b> or external to modem <b>16</b>. Symbol mapper <b>44</b> may map the received encoded data stream to the symbols for the desired modulation. For example, symbol mapper <b>44</b> may map the encoded data stream to the symbols for PM-QPSK modulation to generate the pairs of I′ and Q′ data streams. The I′ and Q′ data streams is used to distinguish the pairs of data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits and pairs of data streams that modem <b>16</b> receives. For example, the I′ and Q′ data streams refer to data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits and the I and Q data streams refer to data stream that modem <b>16</b> receives.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0090\" num=\"0089\">DACs <b>46</b>A-<b>46</b>D receive digital pairs of I′ and Q′ data streams from symbol mapper <b>44</b> and convert the digital data streams into analog data streams for transmission to pluggable photonics module <b>14</b>. For example, DACs <b>46</b>A-<b>46</b>D are output units of modem <b>16</b> that transmit data streams I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ to photonics module <b>14</b>. Photonics module <b>14</b> uses the received data streams from DACs <b>46</b>A-<b>46</b>D to generate a lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> and a lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. Photonics module <b>14</b> then combines these two lightwaves and transmits a single optical signal to network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0091\" num=\"0090\"><figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIGS. 5A and 5B</figref> are block diagrams illustrating examples of a photonics module of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 1</figref> in greater detail. <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5A</figref> illustrates components of photonics module <b>14</b> that receive a PM-QPSK optical signal from network <b>26</b>, convert the optical signal into I/Q electrical data streams, and transmit the I/Q electrical data streams to modem <b>16</b>. <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5B</figref> illustrates components of photonics module <b>14</b> that receive I/Q electrical data streams from modem <b>16</b>, convert the I/Q electrical data streams into a PM-QPSK modulated optical signal, and transmit the optical signal to network <b>26</b>. <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIGS. 5A and 5B</figref> are illustrated separately for ease of description. However, it should be understood that photonics module <b>14</b> includes both the receive photonics illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5A</figref> and the transmit photonics illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5B</figref>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0092\" num=\"0091\">Furthermore, the components of photonics module <b>14</b> are illustrated for PM-QPSK modulation. Photonics module <b>14</b> may include additional, fewer, or different components than those illustrated based on the desired PM-QPSK modulation. In alternate examples, photonics module <b>14</b> includes different components for different modulation schemes. For example, if BPSK modulation is desirable, photonics module <b>14</b> includes components for coherent BPSK modulation. In general, photonics module <b>14</b> includes components needed for the desired type of coherent communication, including even more complex modulation schemes such as multi-level quadrature amplitude modulation (M-QAM where M&gt;4).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0093\" num=\"0092\">As illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5A</figref>, the receive photonics of photonics module <b>14</b> include polarization beam splitter (PBS) <b>48</b>, local oscillator (LO) <b>50</b>, polarization splitter (PS) <b>52</b>, optical hybrid mixers <b>54</b>A and <b>54</b>B, and photo-detectors (PDs) <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D. PDs <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D convert the magnitude of the optical signal to an electrical representation. PBS <b>48</b> receives an optical signal from network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b> and splits the received optical signal into first and second optical signals with nominally orthogonal polarization (e.g., substantially orthogonal polarization). Each one of optical hybrid mixers <b>54</b>A and <b>54</b>B receive respective optical signals from the first and second nominally orthogonal optical signals from PBS <b>48</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0094\" num=\"0093\">The receive photonics also include local oscillator <b>50</b>, which is a laser. Local oscillator <b>50</b> provides the phase reference required in coherent system to recover the PM-QPSK optical waveform that photonics module <b>14</b> receives. In some examples, local oscillator <b>50</b> may be a free running oscillator. For example, the laser signal outputted by local oscillator <b>50</b> may not need to be phase-locked with the optical signal that PBS <b>48</b> receives.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0095\" num=\"0094\">Polarization splitter (PS) <b>52</b> receives the light from local oscillator <b>50</b> and splits the light into (at least) first and second light paths. Each one of optical hybrid mixers <b>54</b>A and <b>54</b>B receive respective local oscillator light from the first and second light paths from the PS <b>52</b>. In some examples, the location of PBS <b>48</b> and PS <b>52</b> may be swapped with no loss of functionality, provided the light from local oscillator <b>50</b> is split into two nominally orthogonally polarized lightwaves.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0096\" num=\"0095\">Optical hybrid mixers <b>54</b>A and <b>54</b>B each mix the respective optical signals from PBS <b>48</b> with the respective local oscillator lightwave reference from PS <b>52</b> and output optical data stream representing in-phase (I) and quadrature-phase (Q) components of the PM-QPSK modulated signal. For example, optical hybrid mixer <b>54</b>A outputs I<sub>1 </sub>and Q<sub>1 </sub>optical data streams. Optical hybrid mixer <b>54</b>B outputs I<sub>2 </sub>and Q<sub>2 </sub>optical data streams. In some examples, optical hybrid mixers <b>54</b>A and <b>54</b>B may be 90 degree optical hybrid mixers. Also, in some examples, each one of the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>2</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>optical data streams may be differentially encoded data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0097\" num=\"0096\">Photo-detectors <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D receive respective optical signals of the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>2</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>optical data streams and convert these optical signals into analog electrical data streams. Photo-detectors <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D may be composed of a single photo-diode or a pair of nominally balanced photo-diodes. A transimpedence amplifier (TIA) element for each photo-detector may used to convert photo-current from the photo-diode(s) to a voltage representation. However, the inclusion of TIA elements may not be necessary in every example. The electrical output of each photo-detector in <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D can be single-ended or differential electrical signals. In some examples, the TIA elements may include automatic gain control (AGC) amplifiers, or the AGC amplifiers may be external to the TIA elements. The AGC amplifiers may nominally maintain output electrical voltage amplitude/swing for varying input electrical current amplitude/swings.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0098\" num=\"0097\">In this manner, the receive photonics of photonics module <b>14</b> convert the PM-QPSK modulated optical signal into electrical I and Q data stream pairs representing the optical PM-QPSK signal for further processing by processor modem <b>16</b>. For example, modem <b>16</b> receives the I/Q electrical data stream pairs from photo-detectors <b>56</b>A-<b>56</b>D.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0099\" num=\"0098\">As illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5B</figref>, the transmit photonics of photonics module <b>14</b> include laser <b>58</b>, polarization splitter (PS) <b>60</b>, modulators <b>62</b>A and <b>62</b>B, and polarization beam combiner (PBC) <b>64</b>. PBC <b>64</b> is coupled to optical link <b>24</b> and outputs an optical modulated signal (e.g., a PM-QPSK modulated optical signal). Also, as illustrated, photonics module <b>14</b> receives I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams, which are electrical data streams are outputted by modem <b>16</b> for PM-QPSK modulation.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0100\" num=\"0099\">In this disclosure, the terms I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams are used to described data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits to photonics module <b>14</b>, and the terms I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams are used to described data streams that modem <b>16</b> receives from photonics module <b>14</b>. The I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits may be different from the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams that modem <b>16</b> receives. For example, the I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams are for downstream communication, while the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>data streams are for upstream communication.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0101\" num=\"0100\">For example, the I<sub>1</sub>′ and Q<sub>1</sub>′ data streams may form a first pair of data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits, and may be for the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>. The I<sub>2</sub>′ and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams may form a second pair of data streams that modem <b>16</b> transmits, and may be for the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. In some examples, the I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams may be composed of differential data streams that are AC coupled via capacitors to photonics module <b>14</b>. In some examples, photonics module <b>14</b> may include drive amplifiers coupled to each one of the I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams. The drive amplifiers may amplify the voltage level of the I<sub>1</sub>′, Q<sub>1</sub>′, I<sub>2</sub>′, and Q<sub>2</sub>′ data streams outputted by modem <b>16</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0102\" num=\"0101\">Laser <b>58</b> may be any type of laser that is usable for high bit rate optical signal transmission, typically a low linewidth laser in the 1550 nm wavelength range (so-called C-Band), but can be any wavelength. Optical amplifiers operating in same wavelength range may allow photonics module <b>14</b> to transmit the generated optical signal a relatively far distance. An example is Erbium-Doped Fiber Amplifiers (EDFAs), which amplify light in the 1550 nm spectral region. The ability of photonics module <b>14</b> to transmit the generated optical signal a relatively far distance reduces the number of intermittent optical-to-electrical-to-optical (O-E-O) repeaters needed to regenerate the transmitted optical signal.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0103\" num=\"0102\">Polarization splitter (PS) <b>60</b> receives the light from laser <b>34</b> and splits the light into (at least) two paths, and may be similar to PS <b>52</b> of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5A</figref>. Each one of modulators <b>62</b>A and <b>62</b>B receives light from one of the paths. Modulators <b>62</b>A and <b>62</b>B modulate the light on the respective paths with respective I/Q electrical data stream pairs. Modulators <b>62</b>A and <b>62</b>B may be referred to as IQ modulators or Cartesian modulators. In the example of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 5B</figref>, modulator <b>62</b>A receives the I<sub>1</sub>′ and Q<sub>1</sub>′ electrical data streams and modulates the light to form a complex modulated lightwave signal, modulated in both magnitude and phase, forming a QPSK signal. Modulator <b>62</b>B receives I<sub>2</sub>′ and Q<sub>2</sub>′ electrical data streams and modulates the light to form a complex modulated lightwave signal, modulated in both magnitude and phase, forming a second QPSK signal.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0104\" num=\"0103\">Polarization beam combiner (PBC) <b>64</b> receives the polarized and modulated optical signals from each one of modulator <b>62</b>A and <b>62</b>B. For instance, the optical QPSK signals from modulators <b>62</b>A or <b>62</b>B are then multiplexed in (nominally orthogonal) polarization using PBC <b>64</b>. For example, PBC <b>64</b> combines the received QPSK optical signals into nominally orthogonal polarizations into a single polarization multiplexed (PM) optical signal and transmits the PM-QPSK optical signal to network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b>. In this manner, photonics module <b>14</b> utilizes lightwave communications techniques to generate and transmit an optical PM-QPSK signal.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0105\" num=\"0104\"><figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 6</figref> is a flow chart illustrating an example technique in accordance with one or more aspects of this disclosure. For purposes of illustration only, reference is made to <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIGS. 1-3</figref>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0106\" num=\"0105\">A first ADC receives a first analog electrical data stream, and a second ADC receives a second analog electrical data stream (<b>66</b>). For example, ADC <b>18</b>A receives a first analog electrical data stream (e.g., I<sub>1</sub>) from photonics module <b>14</b>, and ADC <b>18</b>B receives a second analog electrical data stream (e.g., Q<sub>1</sub>) from photonics module <b>14</b>. In this example, the first and second analog electrical data streams together represent a portion of the optical signal received by photonics module <b>14</b>. For instance, I<sub>1 </sub>and Q<sub>1 </sub>together represent a lightwave of the optical signal with polarization <b>1</b>. Similarly, ADC <b>18</b>C receives a third analog electrical data stream (e.g., I<sub>2</sub>) from photonics module <b>14</b>, and ADC <b>18</b>D receives a fourth analog electrical data stream (e.g., Q<sub>2</sub>) from photonics module <b>14</b>. In this example, the third and fourth analog electrical data streams together represent another portion of the optical signal received by photonics module <b>14</b>. For instance, I<sub>2 </sub>and Q<sub>2 </sub>together represent a lightwave of the optical signal with polarization <b>2</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0107\" num=\"0106\">The first ADC and the second ADC sample the first and second analog electrical data streams to convert the first and second analog electrical data streams to first and second digital electrical data streams (<b>68</b>). For example, ADC <b>18</b>A samples the first analog electrical data stream at a sampling rate that is nominally twice or greater than twice the symbol rate at which photonics module <b>14</b> transmitted the first and second analog electrical data streams to convert the first analog electrical data stream into a first digital electrical data stream at the sampling rate. Similarly, ADC <b>18</b>B samples the second analog electrical data stream at the sampling rate that is nominally twice or greater than twice the symbol rate at which photonics module <b>14</b> transmitted the first and second analog electrical data streams to convert the second analog electrical data stream into a second digital electrical data stream at the sampling rate. ADCs <b>18</b>C and <b>18</b>D perform similar functions with respect to the third and fourth analog electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0108\" num=\"0107\">Furthermore, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may sample their respective analog electrical data streams without the analog electrical data streams being filtered prior to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling their respective analog electrical data streams. For instance, photonics module <b>14</b> may not be coupled to an analog filter that filters the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>analog electrical data streams prior to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>analog electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0109\" num=\"0108\">As an example, photonics module <b>14</b> receives an optical PM-QPSK signal with a symbol rate of 25 Gbaud. Photonics module <b>14</b> converts the optical signal into the I<sub>1</sub>, Q<sub>1</sub>, I<sub>2</sub>, and Q<sub>2 </sub>analog electrical data streams. The symbol rate of these analog electrical data streams is 25 Gsamples/s. In this example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample these analog electrical data streams at a sampling rate that is nominally equal to or greater than 50 Gsamples/s (e.g., nominally twice the symbol rate or greater than twice the symbol rate of these electrical data streams).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0110\" num=\"0109\">A first digital filter and a second digital filter digitally filter the first and second digital electrical data streams (<b>70</b>). For example, digital filter <b>20</b>A digitally filters the first digital electrical data stream to output a first filtered digital electrical data stream at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate at which ADC <b>18</b>A sampled and less than twice the symbol rate of the first and second analog electrical data streams, and greater than or equal to the symbol rate of the first and second analog electrical data streams. Similarly, digital filter <b>20</b>B digitally filters the second digital electrical data stream to output a second filtered digital electrical data stream at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate at which ADC <b>18</b>B sampled and less than twice the symbol rate of the first and second analog electrical data streams, and greater than or equal to the symbol rate of the first and second analog electrical data streams. Digital filters <b>20</b>C and <b>20</b>D perform similar functions with respect to the third and fourth analog electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0111\" num=\"0110\">For instance, keeping with the previous example, the sampling rate of the first and second digital data streams, as converted by ADCs <b>18</b>A and <b>18</b>B, is at 50 Gsamples/s. In this example, the sampling rate of the first and second digital data streams is 50 Gsamples/s. Digital filters <b>20</b>A and <b>20</b>B filter the first and second digital data streams to output filtered digital electrical data streams at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate and greater than twice the symbol rate, which both equal 50 Gsamples/s in this example, and greater than or equal to 25 Gbaud. As one example, the effective sampling rate may be approximately 5/4*25 (i.e., 31.25 GSamples/s).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0112\" num=\"0111\">In examples described in this disclosures, the number of samples that need to be processed per second in the output of digital filters <b>20</b>A and <b>20</b>B is equivalent to the number of samples that need to be processed per second as if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at a sampling rate equal to the effective sampling rate. However, in aspects of this disclosure, because ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample at a sampling rate that is nominally twice or greater than twice the symbol rate, aliasing effects may be minimized the digital data stream that digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D receive. Also, although digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D output filtered data streams at the effective sampling rate, which is less than the sampling rate and twice the symbol rate, the low pass filters within digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may minimize aliasing effects. Accordingly, the data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may require downstream hardware units <b>22</b> to process fewer samples per second as compared to if downstream hardware units <b>22</b> received the digital data streams directly from ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0113\" num=\"0112\">Downstream hardware units <b>22</b> that include at least one component configured to process the digitally filtered first and second digital electrical data streams at a rate that is substantially similar to the effective sampling rate (e.g., equal to the effective sampling rate) (<b>72</b>). For example, CD equalizer <b>28</b>A and timing recover unit <b>30</b> process the digitally filtered first and second electrical data streams at a rate that is substantially similar to the effective sampling rate (e.g., equal to the effective sampling rate). For instance, if the effective sampling rate is 31.25 Gsamples/s, then CD equalizer <b>28</b>A would process 31.25 Gsamples of the digitally filtered first and second electrical data streams per second. Another digital filter is configured to filter the processed digitally filtered first and second digital electrical data streams to output a digital electrical data stream at a further reduced effective sampling rate (<b>74</b>). For example, digital filter <b>40</b> outputs filtered data stream at a reduced effective sampling rate of 25 Gsamples/s.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0114\" num=\"0113\"><figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref> is a graphical diagram illustrating example results in accordance with one or more aspects of this disclosure. In <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref>, the y-axis represents a measure of system performance expressed in Q<sup>2 </sup>factor, where the exponent 2 indicates that the Q factor is using a “20 log” definition such as Q<sup>2 </sup>(dB) equals 20 log<sub>10</sub>(Q<sub>linear</sub>). The x-axis represents the analog bandwidth of the front-end of the ADC such as ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, and is represented as Rx Be in giga-hertz (GHz). The values of <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref> were generated with the symbol rate (R) being 31.625 Gbaud and with PM-QPSK modulation.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0115\" num=\"0114\">The top line in circles represents the system performance where ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample at a sampling rate of at least twice the symbol rate (2*R), and digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D output digital data streams at the sampling rate, and not the effective sampling rate. In other words, the components of modem <b>16</b> operate with the 2*R number of samples per second. The top line may be considered as representing the system performance of an ideal system where the size and power consumption of the components of modem <b>16</b> are not of concern.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0116\" num=\"0115\">The bottom line in squares represents the system performance where the output of photonics module <b>14</b> is low pass filtered with an analog low pass filter prior to the ADCs receiving the analog electrical data streams from photonics module <b>14</b>. In this example, the analog low pass filter is simulated with an analog filter shape of a Bessel-Thompson of 3<sup>rd </sup>order. In the bottom line in squares, the ADCs sample at less than the Nyquist rate because the analog low pass filter low pass filters the output of photonics module <b>14</b>. For purposes of illustration, the bandwidth of the analog low pass filter was selected to be 5/4*R to provide a proper comparison with examples where digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D achieve an effective sampling rate of 5/4*R.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0117\" num=\"0116\">The middle line in diamonds represents the system performance in accordance with one or more example techniques described in this disclosure. For example, the middle line represents the system performance where ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the received analog electrical data streams at a sampling rate of 2*R. Then, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D filter and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate of 5/4*R.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0118\" num=\"0117\">As illustrated, when the analog bandwidth Rx Be is reduced below a certain value (in this example &lt;8 GHz), too much signal frequency content may be filtered and distortion is introduced in the waveform that cannot be compensated by modem <b>16</b> and a severe penalty is shown. Accordingly, in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref>, the top, middle, and bottom lines all indicate poor performance at frequencies less than approximately 8 GHz.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0119\" num=\"0118\">As illustrated in <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref>, for the ideal case, as represented by the top line, for frequencies greater than 8 GHz, the performance is practically constant as a function of Rx Be because the sampling in the ADCs is being done at the Nyquist rate which is not producing aliasing effect. As illustrated in the bottom line, which represents a system where the data streams outputted by photonics module <b>14</b> are analog low pass filtered prior to the ADCs, there are aliasing effects because the sampling rate is less than the Nyquist rate. However, the penalty of the aliasing effects, in the bottom line, is based on the Rx Be value. For example, at optimum Rx Be of 10 GHz, the penalty is about 0.7 dB (i.e., the difference at 10 GHz between the top line and bottom line). However, at RX Be of 22 GHz, where only weak filtering is applied, most of the aliasing effects may not be removed, leading to more than 2 dB penalty compared to the top line.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0120\" num=\"0119\">The middle line, which represents example system performance values for techniques described in this disclosure, illustrates system performance behavior similar to that of the ideal case (e.g., fairly constant as a function of Rx Be). However, there is a slight penalty compared to the ideal case because the number of samples that need to be processed per second in the output of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D is less than the Nyquist rate, which introduces aliasing effects. For example, <figref idref=\"DRAWINGS\">FIG. 7</figref> illustrates a slight constant penalty of approximately 0.4 dB (e.g., the difference between the top line and the middle line) across values of Rx Be. This small penalty may be due to residual aliasing effects that the low pass filters of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may not be able to remove. Nevertheless, the potential benefits of reduced size and power consumption of modem <b>16</b>, which may result in achieving the effective sampling rate in the manner described above, may outweigh the drawbacks associated with a small penalty of 0.4 dB as compared to the ideal situation.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0121\" num=\"0120\">The techniques of this disclosure may be implemented in a wide variety of devices or apparatuses, including line-cards, routers, optical interfaces, an integrated circuit (IC) or a set of ICs (i.e., a chip set). Various components, modules or units are described in this disclosure to emphasize functional aspects of devices configured to perform the disclosed techniques, but do not necessarily require realization by different hardware units. Rather, as described above, various units may be combined in a hardware unit or provided by a collection of interoperative hardware units.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0122\" num=\"0121\">Various examples have been described. These and other examples are within the scope of the following claims.</p>\n",
              "normalized" : "\n<h2 id=\"h-0005\" level=\"\">DETAILED DESCRIPTION</h2>\n<p id=\"p-0021\" num=\"0020\" level=\"\"><a idref=\"FIG-1\" id=\"FR-0001\" class=\"figref\">FIG. 1</a> is a block diagram illustrating an optical communication system <b>10</b>. As illustrated, optical communication system <b>10</b> includes network <b>26</b> coupled to line card <b>12</b> via optical link <b>24</b>. Examples of optical communication system <b>10</b> include, but are not limited to, wavelength-division multiplexing (WDM) systems, including a dense wavelength division multiplexing (DWDM) system. For example, a WDM system includes a plurality of slots reserved for a plurality of line cards, such as line card <b>12</b>. However, aspects of this disclosure are not limited to WDM systems that include line cards. The techniques of this disclosure are extendable to other optical communication systems that require transmission and reception of data. For purposes of illustration only and for ease of description, the examples are described in context of a WDM system.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0022\" num=\"0021\" level=\"\">In WDM systems, for downstream transmission, line card <b>12</b> receives optical signals from network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b> that include data for transmission to one or more devices such as switches and routers. In the reverse, for upstream transmission, line card <b>12</b> receives data from the switches and routers for transmission to network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b>. Examples of network <b>26</b> include, but are not limited to, a wide area network (WAN) or the Internet.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0023\" num=\"0022\" level=\"\">For example, line card <b>12</b> includes photonics module <b>14</b> and modulator/demodulator (modem) <b>16</b>. Photonics module <b>14</b> includes components that receive a lightwave signal from network <b>26</b> via optical link <b>24</b>, and convert the lightwave signal into one or more electrical data streams. Modem <b>16</b> receives the electrical data streams and performs appropriate signal processing such as equalizing optical and electrical impairments, phase tracking, data slicing, and other such signal processing to minimize the number of errors in the data transmitted to the routers and switches from line card <b>12</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0024\" num=\"0023\" level=\"\">As the amount of data that needs to be transmitted to and received from network <b>26</b> increases, the data rate at which line card <b>12</b> needs to forward data to and from the routers and switches increases. For example, routers and switches are being designed to receive and transmit data at ever higher data rates, and the WDM systems need scale to the higher data rates to keep pace with data rates from the routers and switches. For instance, it may have been sufficient for line card <b>12</b> to operate at approximately 10 gigabits per second (Gbps), but now needs to operate at 100 Gbps, and may be even 126.5 Gbps if forward error correction (FEC) is utilized.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0025\" num=\"0024\" level=\"\">Transmitting and receiving data at such relatively high data rates (e.g., 100 Gbps to 126.5 Gbps) may require modulation schemes with multi-level signaling in order to encode more than 1 bit/symbol, which reduces the symbol rate. For example, without multi-level signaling, one symbol represents one bit, and transmitting and receiving data at 100 Gbps or 126.5 Gbps results in transmitting and receiving data at symbol rate of 100 giga-samples (Gsamples) per second (Gsamples/s) or 126.5 Gsamples/s. However, with multi-level signaling, one symbol represents more than one bit, and the symbol rate can be reduced to less than 100 Gsamples/s or 126.5 Gsamples/s.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0026\" num=\"0025\" level=\"\">For example, transmission and reception of data at such relatively high data rates may require quadrature phase-shift keying (QPSK), as one example, although other modulation schemes are possible such as polarization multiplexed QPSK (PM-QPSK). In QPSK, one symbol represents two bits (e.g., encoding of 2 bits/symbol), and in PM-QPSK, one symbol represents four bits (e.g., encoding of 4 bits/symbol). Accordingly, in PM-QPSK, a symbol rate of 25 giga-baud (Gbaud) can represent 100 Gbps of data (e.g., 100 gigabits*1 symbol/4 bits equals 25 Gbaud), and 31.625 Gbaud can represent 126.5 Gbps of data, where one Gbaud equals one Gsample/s.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0027\" num=\"0026\" level=\"\">For purposes of illustration, the example techniques are described with respect to PM-QPSK modulation. However, aspects of this disclosure should not be considered so limiting. The techniques described in this disclosure are extendable to other modulation schemes such as those used for coherent optical communication systems. For instance, BPSK, PM-BPSK, QPSK, PM-QPSK, M-quadrature amplitude modulation (M-QAM) (where M&gt;4), and PM-M-QAM modulation schemes may each require coherent optical detection, and optical communication system <b>10</b> may be considered as a coherent optical communication system.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0028\" num=\"0027\" level=\"\">Coherent optical communication systems refer to optical systems that utilize both magnitude and phase information for transmitting and receiving data such as for phase-shift keying modulation (e.g., BPSK, PM-BPSK, QPSK, PM-QPSK, M-QAM, or PM-M-QAM modulation). For example, in coherent optical communication systems, photonics module <b>14</b> may rely on a beating between a received signal and a local reference which maps both magnitude and phase information of the received optical electric field in the optical signal to measurable voltage or current. For instance, coherent optical communication systems may require using a local carrier phase reference generated at photonics module <b>14</b> for the reception of optical signals from network <b>26</b>. For example, as illustrated in more detail with respect to <a idref=\"FIG-5A\" id=\"FR-0002\" class=\"figref\">FIG. 5A</a>, photonics module <b>14</b> may include optical hybrid mixers to convert the received optical signal into the pairs (e.g., in-phase and quadrature phase) of data streams, referred to as I and Q data streams, for transmission to modem <b>16</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0029\" num=\"0028\" level=\"\">In PSK modulation, binary ones and zeros are represented by changing, or modulating, the phase of a carrier wave sometimes referred to as a lightwave. In this manner, both the magnitude and the phase of the optical signal are used to transmit data. For example, both the magnitude and the phase information of the received optical signal may be needed to recover the transmitted data (e.g., the binary ones and zeros represented by changing or modulating the phase of a carrier wave).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0030\" num=\"0029\" level=\"\">In some examples, in addition, the modulated lightwave in one polarization may be multiplexed with another modulated polarization, which may be orthogonal to the previous one, to produce a polarization multiplexed (PM) signal, such as PM-QPSK. The polarizations of the lightwave signals may be chosen to be orthogonal to allow for a simple polarization beam splitter or polarizer for polarization demultiplexing when photonics module <b>14</b> receives data from network <b>26</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0031\" num=\"0030\" level=\"\">In this way, PM-QPSK may be considered as a combination of two QPSK lightwave signals, where a first QPSK lightwave signal is for a first polarization of the lightwave, and the second QPSK lightwave signal is for a second polarization of the lightwave. Each of the QPSK lightwave signals utilizes four phases to encode two bits per symbol. Accordingly, PM-QPSK modulation utilizes four phases to encode two bits per symbol per polarization, which results in four bits per symbol.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0032\" num=\"0031\" level=\"\">For example, PM-QPSK modulation requires four input electrical data streams per polarization to impart the complex information on the optical carrier. The electrical signal for each polarization contains a pair of in-phase (I) and quadrature (Q) data streams that represent the complex data waveform. For example, in PM-QPSK modulation, there may be two in-phase data streams and two quadrature data streams, and one in-phase (I) data stream and one quadrature (Q) data stream forms one pair of a complex number, and the other I data stream and the other Q data stream forms another pair of a complex number. Each of the in-phase and quadrature data stream pairs may be nominally orthogonal to one another, in polarization, once the electrical data streams impart their complex information on the optical carrier. Each of these I or Q electrical data streams can be single-ended or differential.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0033\" num=\"0032\" level=\"\">In other words, in PM-QPSK modulation, the input optical signal includes two lightwaves that are polarized orthogonally with respect to one another (e.g., one is horizontally polarized light, and the other is vertically polarized light, as an illustrative example). However, the polarization need not always be horizontal and vertical polarized light, and need not always be orthogonal. For ease of description, one of the lightwaves may be referred to as lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>, and the other as lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. Each of the lightwaves may be associated with a particular magnitude and phase. The magnitude and phase of each of the lightwaves may be represented as a complex signal that includes real and imaginary aspects.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0034\" num=\"0033\" level=\"\">For example, for PM-QPSK modulation, photonics module <b>14</b> receives an optical signal via optical link <b>24</b> that includes lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> and lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. Optical components within photonics <b>12</b> extract the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> and the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b> from the received optical signal. The optical components further mix the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> with a lightwave output from a local oscillator within photonics <b>12</b> to generate an in-phase optical data stream, referred to as I₁ to indicate that it is for the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>, and to generate a quadrature optical data stream, referred to as Q₁ to indicate that it is for the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>. The I₁ data stream is proportional to the real aspect of the complex signal of the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>, and the Q₁ data stream is proportional to the imaginary aspect of the complex signal of the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0035\" num=\"0034\" level=\"\">Similarly, the optical components also mix the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b> with a lightwave output from a local oscillator within photonics module <b>14</b> to generate an in-phase optical data stream, referred to as I₂ to indicate that it is for the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>, and to generate a quadrature optical data stream, referred to as Q₂ to indicate that it is for the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. Similar to I₁ and Q₁, the I₂ data stream is proportional to the real aspect of the complex signal of the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>, and the Q₂ data stream is proportional to the imaginary aspect of the complex signal of the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0036\" num=\"0035\" level=\"\">In this manner, the pairs of I/Q optical data streams (e.g., a first pair that includes I₁ and Q₁, and a second pair that includes I₂ and Q₂) together represent the received optical signal. For example, I₁ and Q₁ together represent the specific magnitude and phase of the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b>, and I₂ and Q₂ together represent the specific magnitude and phase of the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b>. Also, in this example, the lightwave with polarization <b>1</b> and the lightwave with polarization <b>2</b> together form the original received optical signal.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0037\" num=\"0036\" level=\"\">Photonics module <b>14</b> also includes components such as photo-detectors and transimpedance amplifiers that convert the I₁, Q₁, I₂, and Q₂ optical data streams into electrical data streams. For example, <a idref=\"FIG-1\" id=\"FR-0003\" class=\"figref\">FIG. 1</a> illustrates photonics module <b>14</b> transmitting the I₁, Q₁, I₂, and Q₂ electrical data streams to modem <b>16</b>. Modem <b>16</b> may be considered as a processor. For instance, examples of modem <b>16</b> include, but are not limited to, a digital signal processor (DSP), a general purpose microprocessor, an application specific integrated circuit (ASIC), a field programmable logic array (FPGA), a combination thereof, or other equivalent integrated or discrete logic circuitry.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0038\" num=\"0037\" level=\"\">Modem <b>16</b> includes analog-to-digital converters (ADCs) <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, digital filters (DFs) <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D, and one or more downstream hardware units <b>22</b>. ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receive respective electrical data streams from photonics module <b>14</b>. For example, ADC <b>14</b>A receives the I₁ electrical data stream, ADC <b>14</b>B receives the Q₁ electrical data stream, ADC <b>14</b>C receives the I₂ electrical data stream, and ADC <b>14</b>D receives the Q₂ electrical data stream. Each of the I/Q electrical data stream pairs are analog signals that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D convert to digital signals. Modem <b>16</b> is configured to recover the magnitude and phase of the received optical signal. In this manner, modem <b>16</b> recovers the data in the optical signal received by photonics module <b>14</b>.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0039\" num=\"0038\" level=\"\">As described above, PM-QPSK modulation may encode four bits per symbol. Accordingly, with PM-QPSK, 100 Gbps translates to a symbol rate of 25 Gbaud (100 Gbps divided by 4), and 126.5 Gbps translates to a symbol rate of 31.625 Gbaud (126.5 Gbps divided by 4). In this example, the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receive is 25 Gbaud (i.e., 25 Gsamples/s) or 31.625 Gbaud, if forward error correction (FEC) is used.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0040\" num=\"0039\" level=\"\">To convert the analog electrical data streams into digital data streams, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the analog I and Q electrical data streams, and for each sample, assign the sample a value proportional the ADC resolution, which may be referred to as the number of bits of resolution. In the techniques described in this disclosure, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the analog I and Q electrical data streams nominally at or beyond the Nyquist rate to minimize aliasing effect. The Nyquist rate is two times the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0041\" num=\"0040\" level=\"\">The term “nominally” may mean approximately. For example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may sample analog I and Q electrical data streams at a rate that is slightly less than the Nyquist rate (e.g., slightly less than twice the symbol rate), at the Nyquist rate, or greater than the Nyquist rate. In this disclosure, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling analog I and Q electrical data streams at a rate that is slightly less than twice the symbol rate or at the symbol rate may be considered as ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling analog I and Q electrical data streams at nominally twice the symbol rate.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0042\" num=\"0041\" level=\"\">As one example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the analog I and Q electrical data streams at a sampling rate of 50 giga-samples per second (Gsamples/s) (i.e., 2*25 Gsamples/s) or 63.25 Gsamples/s (i.e., 2*31.625 Gsamples/s) if FEC is used. In this example, the sampling rate is twice the symbol rate. As another example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may sample the analog I and Q electrical data streams at a sampling rate greater than twice the symbol rate (e.g., 3*25 Gsamples/s or 3*31.625 Gsamples/s, although any value greater than two may be possible). In some cases, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may sample the analog I and Q electrical data streams at a sampling rate that is slightly less than twice the symbol rate (e.g., slightly less than 50 Gsamples/s or 63.25 Gsamples/s).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0043\" num=\"0042\" level=\"\">As one example, the sampling rate that is slightly less than twice the symbol rate may be approximately within 10% of twice the symbol rate. However, the example of approximately within 10% of twice the symbol rate for the sampling rate is provided only for illustration, and is not limiting. The amount by which the sampling rate of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D can be reduced to less than the twice the symbol rate may be based on design choice, such as error rate tolerance, and other design choice criteria.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0044\" num=\"0043\" level=\"\">While sampling at nominally the Nyquist rate or greater may minimize aliasing effects, the amount of samples that needs to be processed per second may be relatively large. For example, if the sampling rate of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D is 50 Gsamples/s, then the output of each one of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D is a digital electrical data stream of 50 Gsamples/s. In some examples, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D represent each of the samples with a plurality of bits, which indicates the linear resolution of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D. For instance, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may represent each of the samples with 6 bits of linear resolution (i.e., 6 bits represent one sample of the received analog electrical data stream as sampled by ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D). In this example, if each one of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D outputs a digital electrical data stream of 50 Gsamples/s, then each one of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may be considered as outputting 300 Gbps (i.e., 50 Gsamples/s*6 bits/sample equals 300 Gbps).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0045\" num=\"0044\" level=\"\">In general, the techniques described in this disclosure are extendable to any resolution of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, and the 6 bits per sample linear resolution is provided for purposes of illustration only. For purposes of clarity, the techniques described in this disclosure are described in context of the amount of data that modem <b>16</b> needs to process per unit of time (e.g., 50 Gsamples/s or 63.25 Gsamples/s) of the digital electrical data streams rather than the bits per second outputted by ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, which is a function of the linear resolution. For example, in a first example, the linear resolution of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may be 6 bits, and in a second example, the linear resolution of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may be 4 bits. In both the first and second example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may sample at a sampling rate of nominally or greater than the Nyquist rate (e.g., 50 Gsamples/s or 63.25 Gsamples/s) to output digital electrical data streams that would need to be processed at 50 Gsamples/s or 63.25 Gsamples/s, in this example. However, in the first example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D each output digital electrical data streams of 300 Gbps or 379.5 Gbps, and in the second example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D each output digital electrical data streams of 200 Gbps or 253 Gbps. Because the number of samples per second in the output of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D may be the same independent of the linear resolution, the techniques are described in context of the number of samples per second that need to be processed.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0046\" num=\"0045\" level=\"\">Without digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D, components of modem <b>16</b> that are further downstream from ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D (e.g., downstream hardware units <b>22</b>) would need to process 4×50 Gsamples/s or 4×63.25 Gsamples/s (e.g., 50 or 63.25 Gsamples for each one of I₁, Q₁, I₂, and Q₂), in this example. In examples where the sampling rate is 50 or 63.25 Gsamples/s, processing such relatively large amount of samples per second may require downstream hardware units <b>22</b> of modem <b>16</b> to be larger in size and consume more power compared to if there were less samples of data that needed processing.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0047\" num=\"0046\" level=\"\">For example, if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at much less than the Nyquist rate, there would be fewer samples that needed to be processed per second. For instance, if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at 25 Gsamples/s, there would 4×25 Gsamples that would need to be processed per second. However, in this case, aliasing effects would dominate, if the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams is 25 Gbaud, making it difficult for modem <b>16</b> to recover the data encoded in the optical signal received by photonics module <b>14</b>. Therefore, it may be desirable to sample at nominally the Nyquist rate or higher to mitigate aliasing effects, while at the same time, it may be desirable to minimize the number of samples of data that needs to be processed to reduce the size and power consumption of modem <b>16</b>. As described in more detail, the example techniques described in disclosure provide for a scheme where the aliasing effects are minimized, and the amount of samples that needs to be processed is minimized.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0048\" num=\"0047\" level=\"\">As illustrated in <a idref=\"FIG-1\" id=\"FR-0004\" class=\"figref\">FIG. 1</a>, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D receive respective digital data streams from ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D. Digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may be considered as filtering the digital electrical data streams received from ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D to output at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate at which ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled and less than twice the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams received by ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, and greater than or equal to the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams received by ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D. Digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D outputting filtered digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate refers to a rate at which ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D would have outputted data streams had ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at a sampling rate that is substantially similar to the effective sampling rate. However, the filtered digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may not suffer from aliasing effects which would have occurred had ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at a sampling rate that is substantially similar to the effective sampling rate without an analog filter filtering the electrical data streams, in the analog domain, prior to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receiving respective electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0049\" num=\"0048\" level=\"\">As an example, assume the symbol rate of the analog electrical data streams outputted by photonics module <b>14</b> equals R. In this example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receive analog electrical data streams having a symbol rate of R, and sample the analog electrical data streams at a sampling rate of 2*R, which is represented as Rs (i.e., Rs=2*R). Each one of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D output a digital data stream, where each of the digital data streams include at least 2*R samples for processing per second. In some example techniques described in this disclosure, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate of less than 2*R, but greater than or equal to R. For example, if the effective sampling rate of the output from digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D is N, then N is less than 2*R, and greater than or equal to R (i.e., R≤N&lt;2*R).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0050\" num=\"0049\" level=\"\">As another example, assume that the sampling rate is 1.999*R, where R is the symbol rate. The sampling rate of 1.999*R may be considered as nominally twice the symbol rate. In this example, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate of less than 1.999*R (e.g., R≤N&lt;1.999*R).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0051\" num=\"0050\" level=\"\">As yet another example, assume that the sampling rate is 3*R, where R is the symbol rate. The sampling rate of 3*R is greater than twice the symbol rate. In this example, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate of less than twice the symbol rate, and greater than or equal to the symbol rate (i.e., R≤N&lt;2*R).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0052\" num=\"0051\" level=\"\">In other words, in examples where the sampling rate is equal to twice the symbol rate or slightly less than twice the symbol rate (i.e., where the sampling rate is nominally twice the symbol rate), digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate. In examples where the sampling rate is greater than twice the symbol rate, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate that is less than twice the symbol rate. Accordingly, to cover examples where the sampling rate is nominally twice the symbol rate, and to cover examples where the sampling rate is greater than twice the symbol rate, this disclosure may describe digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D as digitally filtering the digital data streams and output filtered digital data streams at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate (to cover the nominally twice the symbol rate example) and less than twice the symbol rate of the first and second analog electrical data streams (to cover the greater than twice the symbol rate example).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0053\" num=\"0052\" level=\"\">To understand the effective sampling rate, assume that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled respective analog electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate N, where N is much less than 2*R and greater than or equal to R. In this example, the digital data stream outputted by each one of <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D would include N samples for processing per second, which would be less than the number of samples that need processing per second if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at 2*R (i.e., processing N samples per second is less than processing 2*R samples per second because N is less than 2*R). However, in this case, because ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at much less than 2*R, aliasing effects may dominate making it difficult to recover the data from the received optical signal.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0054\" num=\"0053\" level=\"\">In this disclosure, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may be considered as outputting filtered digital electrical data streams that need to be processed at a rate that is substantially similar to a rate at which the data streams would need to be processed had ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at the effective sampling rate. However, the filtered digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may suffer minimally from aliasing effects because ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled at a sampling rate that is nominally 2*R or greater than 2*R, and not at a sampling rate equal to the effective sampling rate N. To allow ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D to sample at the effective sampling rate, while minimizing aliasing, would have required low pass filtering the analog electrical data streams in the analog domain with anti-aliasing filters prior to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receiving the analog electrical data streams, as is done in some other techniques described below. However, as described in more detail below, filtering in the analog domain with analog anti-aliasing filters may result in poorer performance as compared to filtering in the digital domain with digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0055\" num=\"0054\" level=\"\">As an illustrative example, assume that the symbol rate R is 25 Gbaud. In this example, ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the analog electrical data streams at 50 Gsamples/s. Also, assume that digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D output filtered digital electrical data streams at an effective sampling rate of 31.25 Gsamples/s. In this example, the rate at which the output of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D need to be processed is 31.25 Gsamples/s, which is as if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled the analog electrical data streams at 31.25 Gsamples/s. However, if ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D were to have sampled the analog electrical data streams at 31.25 Gsamples/s, then aliasing effects would dominate. With ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling at the sampling rate of 50 Gsamples/s, and digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D filtering the digital electrical data streams to output filtered digital electrical data streams at 31.25 Gsamples/s (e.g., the effective sampling rate), the techniques described in this disclosure may reduce the number of samples that need to be processed per second, while minimizing aliasing effects in the data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0056\" num=\"0055\" level=\"\">In some examples, the effective sampling rate N may be approximately 5/4*R; although, aspects of this disclosure are not so limited. In coherent optical communication systems, the data is encoded in the magnitude and/or phase of the optical signal. If the magnitude and/or phase of the optical signal cannot be reliably recovered by downstream hardware units <b>22</b> of modem <b>16</b>, the transmitted data cannot be reliably recovered, thereby causing an increase in the BER. In some examples, outputting filtered digital electrical data streams at approximately 5/4*R may minimize the amount of data that downstream hardware units <b>22</b> need to process, while causing only a small BER penalty due to the aliasing effect if appropriate anti-aliasing filters are used.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0057\" num=\"0056\" level=\"\">Digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may be considered as anti-aliasing filters, and particularly, anti-aliasing filters that function in the digital domain. For example, as discussed above, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D output filtered digital electrical data streams at less than the sampling rate and less than the Nyquist rate (i.e., less than twice the symbol rate). The reduction in the amount of data that needs processing may introduce aliasing effects in the resulting data stream. In examples described in this disclosures, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D perform filtering functions that minimize the aliasing effect. Therefore, these filtering functions of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may be considered as performing anti-aliasing functions. As described in more detail, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D implement the filtering functions digitally, rather than in the analog domain. For example, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D implement the filtering functions on the digital data stream outputs of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, rather than on the analog data stream inputs of ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0058\" num=\"0057\" level=\"\">Digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may perform decimation like functions, but the effective sampling rate of the digital data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D is less than the sampling rate at which ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampled, and less than two times the symbol rate (e.g., less than 2*R), rather than equal to 2*R. Also, the effective sampling rate may be in the Gsamples/s range rather than the kilo or mega samples/s range. For example, decimation is sometimes used to refer to the process of reducing the sampling rate. In techniques described in this disclosure, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D receive digital electrical data streams sampled at a sampling rate that is nominally 2*R or greater than 2*R, and output digital electrical data streams with less than 2*R samples per second of data and with less that the number of samples from ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sampling at the sampling rate, and therefore may be considered as performing functions analogous to reducing the sampling rate (i.e., decimation).</p>\n<p id=\"p-0059\" num=\"0058\" level=\"\">However, in some other cases, the term decimation is used in context where the sampling rate was greater than 2*R, and decimation is used to reduce the sampling rate to equal 2*R. In the example techniques described in this disclosure, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may output filtered digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate that is less than 2*R. Furthermore, in some other cases, the term decimation is used to refer to decimating sampling rates in the kilo or mega samples/s range. However, in the example techniques described in this disclosure, the sampling rate may be in the range of 50 Gsamples/s and 63.25 Gsamples/s. Therefore, the term decimation is used as an illustrative term to assist with understanding, and should not be used as a term to limit the techniques described in this disclosure.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0060\" num=\"0059\" level=\"\">There may be various ways in which digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D digitally filter the digital electrical data streams to output filtered digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate N, where N is less than 2*R and less than the sampling rate, and greater than or equal to R. For purposes of illustration only, the following are a few example techniques that digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may implement. These techniques should not be considered limiting, and the techniques described in this disclosure are not limited to any particular technique that digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D implement for digitally filtering the digital electrical data streams to output filtered digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate N.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0061\" num=\"0060\" level=\"\">As one example, each one of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may include a low pass filter and a downsampler. The low pass filter may be implemented as a finite impulse response (FIR) or infinite impulse response (IIR) filter. The bandwidth of the low pass filter may be substantially equal to the desired effective sampling rate. In these examples, the low pass filter may be considered as an anti-aliasing filter that minimizes aliasing effects in the filtered digital electrical data streams outputted by digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D at the effective sampling rate which is less than the Nyquist rate. The downsampler may remove digital bits from the low pass filtered electrical data stream to achieve the effective sampling rate.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0062\" num=\"0061\" level=\"\">However, the above example technique to achieve the effective sampling rate may only allow achieving effective sampling rate that are integer factors of the symbol rate. To achieve the effective sampling rate that is a fractional factor (e.g., 5/4*R) of the symbol rate, each one of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may include an upsampler, a low pass filter, and a downsampler. The upsampler upsamples the received electrical data stream to increase the amount of data that needs to be processed per second. The low pass filter low pass filters the upsampled electrical data stream, and may be considered as the anti-aliasing filter, and the downsampler removes digital bits from the low pass filtered electrical data stream to achieve the effective sampling rate.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0063\" num=\"0062\" level=\"\">As an illustrative example where digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D include an upsampler, a low pass filter, and a downsampler, assume that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D sample the analog electrical data streams at 2*R, where R is the symbol rate. Therefore, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D receive digital data streams sampled at 2*R. Also, assume that the desired effective sampling rate is 5/4*R. In this example, the upsampler of digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may upsample the received digital data stream by a factor of 5 so that the number of samples that need to be processed per second is 10*R. The low pass filter (e.g., the FIR or IIR low pass filter) low pass filters the upsampled digital data stream with a bandwidth of 5/4*R/2. The downsampler may then keep every 8<sup>th </sup>digital sample and remove the 7 digital samples that are between every 8<sup>th </sup>digital sample. In this manner, with upsampling, low pass filtering, and downsampling, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D output filtered digital electrical data streams with 10*R/8 samples that need to be processed per second, which is mathematically equivalent to achieving the effective sampling rate of 5/4*R.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0064\" num=\"0063\" level=\"\">As another example technique for outputting filtered digital electrical data streams at the effective sampling rate, digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D may utilize a polynomials interpolation scheme. One example of polynomial interpolation scheme is described in F. M. Gardner, “Interpolation in Digital Modems—Part I: Fundamentals,” IEEE Transactions on Communications, vol. 41, No. 3, March 1993, and is incorporated by reference in its entirety.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0065\" num=\"0064\" level=\"\">In this manner, the example techniques described in this disclosure sample the analog electrical data streams outputted by photonics module <b>14</b>, via ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D, at a sampling rate that is nominally twice the symbol rate and greater than twice the symbol rate to mitigate aliasing effects. The techniques then digitally filter, with digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D, the resulting data streams to output filtered data streams at an effective sampling rate that is less than the sampling rate and less than twice the symbol rate, and greater than or equal to the symbol rate to reduce the rate at which subsequent components (e.g., downstream hardware units <b>22</b>) within modem <b>16</b> need to process the filtered data streams. This may reduce the amount of samples that downstream hardware units <b>22</b> need to process per second, which in turn may reduce the amount of power that downstream hardware units <b>22</b> consume as compared to examples where digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D do not output data streams at the effective sampling rate. Also, with a reduction in the amount of samples that downstream hardware units <b>22</b> need to process per second, the size of downstream hardware units <b>22</b> may be reduced compared to examples where digital filters <b>20</b>A-<b>20</b>D do not output data streams at the effective sampling rate.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0066\" num=\"0065\" level=\"\">In the example techniques described in this disclosure, the frequency of the analog I and Q electrical data streams that ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receive may be substantially the same as the frequency of the analog I and Q electrical data streams that photonics module <b>14</b> transmits. For example, the analog I and Q electrical data streams may not be low pass filtered with an analog low pass filter prior to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D receiving analog I and Q electrical data streams.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0067\" num=\"0066\" level=\"\">For instance, to reduce the number of samples that need to be processed per second, some other techniques utilize anti-aliasing filters in the analog domain to low pass filter the analog electrical data streams received from photonics module <b>14</b>. Then, ADCs in these other techniques sample the analog low pass filtered electrical data streams at a sampling rate less than the Nyquist rate (e.g., less than 2*R). In this case, the analog low pass filter functions as an anti-aliasing filter in the analog domain and, with proper choice of the low pass bandwidth and filter shape, the aliasing effects attendant in sampling at less than the Nyquist rate can be minimized.</p>\n<p id=\"p-0068\" num=\"0067\" level=\"\">The ADCs in these other techniques may consume less power compared to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D because the ADCs in these other techniques sample at a lower sampling rate (e.g., less than 2*R) compared to ADCs <b>18</b>A-<b>18</b>D that sample at a sampling rate that is nominally 2*R or greater than 2*R.
